          <img alt="I-35W.svg" data-file-height="601" data-file-width="751" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/I-35W.svg/25px-I-35W.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/I-35W.svg/38px-I-35W.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/I-35W.svg/50px-I-35W.svg.png 2x" width="25"/>
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Interstate_345" title="Interstate 345">
          <img alt="I-345.svg" data-file-height="601" data-file-width="751" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/I-345.svg/25px-I-345.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/I-345.svg/38px-I-345.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/I-345.svg/50px-I-345.svg.png 2x" width="25"/>
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Interstate_635_(Texas)" title="Interstate 635 (Texas)">
          <img alt="I-635.svg" data-file-height="601" data-file-width="751" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/I-635.svg/25px-I-635.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/I-635.svg/38px-I-635.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/I-635.svg/50px-I-635.svg.png 2x" width="25"/>
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Interstate_820" title="Interstate 820">
          <img alt="I-820.svg" data-file-height="601" data-file-width="751" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/I-820.svg/25px-I-820.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/I-820.svg/38px-I-820.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/I-820.svg/50px-I-820.svg.png 2x" width="25"/>
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        Dallas–Fort Worth–Arlington, TX Metropolitan Statistical Area
       </b>
       , the official title designated by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="United States Office of Management and Budget">
        United States Office of Management and Budget
       </a>
       , encompasses 13 counties within the U.S. state of
       <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">
        Texas
       </a>
       . Residents of the area refer to it as the
       <b>
        Dallas/Fort Worth Metroplex
       </b>
       ,
       <b>
        DFW
       </b>
       , or
       <b>
        The Metroplex
       </b>
       . It is the economic and cultural hub of the region commonly called
       <a href="/wiki/North_Texas" title="North Texas">
        North Texas
       </a>
       or North Central Texas and the largest inland metropolitan area in the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The population of the Dallas–Fort Worth Metroplex is 7,233,323 according to the 2016
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Census" title="U.S. Census">
        U.S. Census
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       making it the largest metropolitan area in
       <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">
        Texas
       </a>
       , the largest in the
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">
        South
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Metropolitan_Statistical_Areas" title="List of Metropolitan Statistical Areas">
        fourth-largest
       </a>
       in the United States, and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_the_Americas_by_population" title="List of metropolitan areas in the Americas by population">
        tenth-largest
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">
        Americas
       </a>
       . In 2016, DFW ascended to the number one spot in the nation in year-over-year population growth.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2016, the metropolitan economy surpassed
       <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">
        Houston, Texas
       </a>
       to become the fourth largest in the U.S., with a 2016 real GDP just under $512 billion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As such, the metropolitan area's economy is ranked
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_GDP" title="List of cities by GDP">
        10th largest
       </a>
       in the world. In 2013, the metropolitan area led the nation with the largest year-over-year increase in employment and advanced to become the fourth-largest employment center in the nation (behind
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">
        New York City
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">
        Los Angeles
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">
        Chicago
       </a>
       ) with more than three million non-farm jobs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of January 2017, the metropolitan job count has increased to 3,558,200 jobs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The city's economy is primarily based on banking, commerce, telecommunications, technology, energy, healthcare and medical research, and transportation and logistics. In 2017, Dallas–Fort Worth is home to 22
       <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">
        Fortune 500
       </a>
       companies, the third-largest concentration of
       <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">
        Fortune 500
       </a>
       companies in the nation (behind
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">
        New York City
       </a>
       (63) and
       <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">
        Chicago
       </a>
       (34)).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Metroplex" title="Metroplex">
        metroplex
       </a>
       encompasses 9,286 square miles (24,100 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ) of total area: 8,991 sq mi (23,290 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ) is land, while 295 sq mi (760 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ) is water, making it larger in area than the
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">
        U.S. states
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">
        Rhode Island
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">
        Connecticut
       </a>
       combined.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Origin_of_the_term">
        Origin of the term
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Origin of the term">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Metroplex" title="Metroplex">
        Metroplex
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       A
       <a href="/wiki/Portmanteau" title="Portmanteau">
        portmanteau
       </a>
       of
       <i>
        metropolis
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        complex
       </i>
       , the term
       <i>
        metroplex
       </i>
       is credited to Harve Chapman, an executive vice president with Dallas-based Tracy-Locke which was one of three advertising agencies that worked with the North Texas Commission (NTC) on strategies to market the region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The NTC copyrighted
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NTCHistory_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NTCHistory-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the term "Southwest Metroplex" in 1972 as a replacement for the previously-ubiquitous "North Texas", which studies had shown lacked identifiability outside the state. In fact, only 38 percent of a survey group identified Dallas and Fort Worth as part of "North Texas", with the
       <a href="/wiki/Texas_Panhandle" title="Texas Panhandle">
        Texas Panhandle
       </a>
       also a perceived correct answer, being the northernmost region of Texas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NTC_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NTC-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span id="Metroplex_cities.2C_towns.2C_and_CDPs">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Metroplex_cities,_towns,_and_CDPs">
        Metroplex cities, towns, and CDPs
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Metroplex cities, towns, and CDPs">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Note: Cities and towns are categorized based on the latest population estimates from the
       <a href="/wiki/North_Central_Texas_Council_of_Governments" title="North Central Texas Council of Governments">
        North Central Texas Council of Governments
       </a>
       (as of January 1, 2017).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       No population estimates are released for
       <a href="/wiki/Census-designated_place" title="Census-designated place">
        census-designated places
       </a>
       (CDPs), which are marked with an asterisk (*). These places are categorized based on their 2010 census population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Places_with_more_than_100.2C000_inhabitants">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Places_with_more_than_100,000_inhabitants">
        Places with more than 100,000 inhabitants
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Places with more than 100,000 inhabitants">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dallas_Metropolitan_Area_at_Night.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="720" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Dallas_Metropolitan_Area_at_Night.jpg/350px-Dallas_Metropolitan_Area_at_Night.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Dallas_Metropolitan_Area_at_Night.jpg/525px-Dallas_Metropolitan_Area_at_Night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Dallas_Metropolitan_Area_at_Night.jpg/700px-Dallas_Metropolitan_Area_at_Night.jpg 2x" width="350"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dallas_Metropolitan_Area_at_Night.jpg" title="Enlarge">

      <p>
       As of the 2010 United States
       <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">
        census
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR2_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-GR2-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       there were 6,371,773 people. The racial makeup of the MSA was 50.2%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Whites" title="Whites">
        White
       </a>
       , 15.4%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American_(U.S._Census)" title="African American (U.S. Census)">
        African American
       </a>
       , 0.6%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_American_(U.S._Census)" title="Native American (U.S. Census)">
        Native American
       </a>
       , 5.9%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_(U.S._Census)" title="Asian (U.S. Census)">
        Asian
       </a>
       , 0.1%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_(U.S._Census)" title="Pacific Islander (U.S. Census)">
        Pacific Islander
       </a>
       , 10.0% from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">
        other races
       </a>
       , and 2.4% from two or more races.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_(U.S._Census)" title="Hispanic (U.S. Census)">
        Hispanic
       </a>
       or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" title="Latino (U.S. Census)">
        Latino
       </a>
       of any race were 27.5% of the population.
      </p>
      <p>
       The median income for a household in the MSA was $48,062, and the median income for a family was $55,263. Males had a median income of $39,581 versus $27,446 for females. The
       <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">
        per capita income
       </a>
       for the MSA was $21,839.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Combined_Statistical_Area">
        Combined Statistical Area
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Combined Statistical Area">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The Dallas–Fort Worth, TX–OK Combined Statistical Area is made up of 20 counties in north central Texas and one county in southern Oklahoma. The statistical area includes two
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_metropolitan_area" title="United States metropolitan area">
        metropolitan areas
       </a>
       and seven
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_micropolitan_area" title="United States micropolitan area">
        micropolitan areas
       </a>
       . As of the 2010 Census, the CSA had a population of 6,817,483 (though a July 1, 2015 estimate placed the population at 7,504,362).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstCSA_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-PopEstCSA-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The CSA definition encompasses 14,628 sq mi (37,890 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ) of area, of which 14,126 sq mi (36,590 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ) is land and 502 sq mi (1,300 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ) is water.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Components">
        Components
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Components">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <b>
        Metropolitan Statistical Areas (MSAs)
       </b>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Dallas–Fort Worth–Arlington (Collin, Dallas,
        <a href="/wiki/Denton_County,_Texas" title="Denton County, Texas">
         Denton
        </a>
        , Ellis, Hunt, Hood, Johnson, Kaufman, Parker, Rockwall, Somervell, Tarrant, and Wise counties)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sherman-Denison_metropolitan_area" title="Sherman-Denison metropolitan area">
         Sherman-Denison
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Grayson_County,_Texas" title="Grayson County, Texas">
         Grayson County
        </a>
        )
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       <b>
        Micropolitan Statistical Areas (μSAs)
       </b>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Athens (
        <a href="/wiki/Henderson_County,_Texas" title="Henderson County, Texas">
         Henderson County
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        Bonham (
        <a href="/wiki/Fannin_County,_Texas" title="Fannin County, Texas">
         Fannin County
        </a>
        ) (delineated and added in 2015)
       </li>
       <li>
        Corsicana (
        <a href="/wiki/Navarro_County,_Texas" title="Navarro County, Texas">
         Navarro County
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        Durant, OK (
        <a href="/wiki/Bryan_County,_Oklahoma" title="Bryan County, Oklahoma">
         Bryan County, Oklahoma
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        Gainesville (
        <a href="/wiki/Cooke_County,_Texas" title="Cooke County, Texas">
         Cooke County
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        Mineral Wells (
        <a href="/wiki/Palo_Pinto_County,_Texas" title="Palo Pinto County, Texas">
         Palo Pinto County
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        Sulphur Springs (
        <a href="/wiki/Hopkins_County,_Texas" title="Hopkins County, Texas">
         Hopkins County
        </a>
        )
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Note: The
       <a href="/wiki/Granbury_micropolitan_area" title="Granbury micropolitan area">
        Granbury micropolitan statistical area
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Hood_County,_Texas" title="Hood County, Texas">
        Hood
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Somervell_County,_Texas" title="Somervell County, Texas">
        Somervell
       </a>
       counties) was made part of the Dallas–Fort Worth–Arlington, Texas Metropolitan Statistical Area effective 2013.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics_2">
        Demographics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Demographics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       As of the
       <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">
        census
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR2_17-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-GR2-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       of 2000, there were 5,487,956 people, 2,006,665 households, and 1,392,540 families residing within the CSA. The racial makeup of the CSA was 70.41%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_(U.S._Census)" title="White (U.S. Census)">
        White
       </a>
       , 13.34%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American_(U.S._Census)" title="African American (U.S. Census)">
        African American
       </a>
       , 0.59%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_American_(U.S._Census)" title="Native American (U.S. Census)">
        Native American
       </a>
       , 3.58%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_(U.S._Census)" title="Asian (U.S. Census)">
        Asian
       </a>
       , 0.08%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_(U.S._Census)" title="Pacific Islander (U.S. Census)">
        Pacific Islander
       </a>
       , 9.62% from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">
        other races
       </a>
       , and 2.39% from two or more races.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_(U.S._Census)" title="Hispanic (U.S. Census)">
        Hispanic
       </a>
       or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" title="Latino (U.S. Census)">
        Latino
       </a>
       of any race were 20.83% of the population. It is home to the fourth-largest
       <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">
        Muslim
       </a>
       population in the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The median income for a household in the CSA was $43,836, and the median income for a family was $50,898. Males had a median income of $37,002 versus $25,553 for females. The
       <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">
        per capita income
       </a>
       for the CSA was $20,460.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">

          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">

         </div>
        </td>

      </table>
      <p>
       The Metroplex overlooks mostly
       <a href="/wiki/Prairie" title="Prairie">
        prairie
       </a>
       land with a few rolling hills dotted by man-made lakes cut by streams, creeks and rivers surrounded by forest land. The Metroplex is situated in the
       <a href="/wiki/Texas_blackland_prairies" title="Texas blackland prairies">
        Texas blackland prairies
       </a>
       region, so named for its fertile black soil found especially in the rural areas of Collin, Dallas, Ellis, Hunt, Kaufman, and Rockwall counties.
      </p>
      <p>
       Many areas of Denton, Johnson, Parker, Tarrant, and Wise counties are located in the Fort Worth
       <a href="/wiki/Cross_Timbers#29d:_Grand_Prairie" title="Cross Timbers">
        Prairie
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       region of North Texas, which has less fertile and more rocky soil than that of the Texas blackland prairie; most of the rural land on the Fort Worth Prairie is ranch land. A large onshore
       <a href="/wiki/Shale_gas" title="Shale gas">
        natural gas
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_field" title="Natural gas field">
        field
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Barnett_Shale" title="Barnett Shale">
        Barnett Shale
       </a>
       , lies underneath this area; Denton, Tarrant and Wise counties feature many
       <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">
        natural gas
       </a>
       wells. Continuing land use change results in scattered crop fields surrounded by residential or commercial development.
      </p>
      <p>
       South of Dallas and Fort Worth is a line of rugged hills that goes north to south about 15 miles (24 km) that looks similar to the
       <a href="/wiki/Texas_Hill_Country" title="Texas Hill Country">
        Texas Hill Country
       </a>
       200 miles (320 km) to the south.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">

       <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_in_the_Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex" title="List of companies in the Dallas–Fort Worth metroplex">
        List of companies in the Dallas–Fort Worth metroplex
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AMRHeadquartersFortWorth0.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="453" data-file-width="800" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/AMRHeadquartersFortWorth0.jpg/220px-AMRHeadquartersFortWorth0.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/AMRHeadquartersFortWorth0.jpg/330px-AMRHeadquartersFortWorth0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/AMRHeadquartersFortWorth0.jpg/440px-AMRHeadquartersFortWorth0.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AMRHeadquartersFortWorth0.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Headquarters of
         <a href="/wiki/AMR_Corporation" title="AMR Corporation">
          AMR Corporation
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">
          American Airlines
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The cities of Dallas and Fort Worth are the two central cities of the Metroplex, with Arlington being a third economically important city; it is a center for sporting events, tourism and manufacturing. Most other incorporated cities in the Metroplex are "bedroom communities" serving largely as residential and small-business centers, though there are several key employers in these regions. Due to the large number of smaller, less well-known cities, Metroplex residents commonly divide the region roughly in half along Texas
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_35" title="Interstate 35">
        Interstate 35
       </a>
       , which runs north-south, splitting into two 'branches' (
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_35E_(Texas)" title="Interstate 35E (Texas)">
        I-35E
       </a>
       in Dallas and
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_35W_(Texas)" title="Interstate 35W (Texas)">
        I-35W
       </a>
       in Fort Worth) through the Metroplex. They refer to places as being on the "Dallas side" or the "Fort Worth side", or in "the Arlington area," which is almost directly south of the airport. It is nominally between the two major east-west interstates in the region (I-20, passing to the south of both downtowns, and I-30, connecting Dallas and Fort Worth city centers).
      </p>
      <p>
       Dallas and its suburbs have one of the highest concentrations of corporate headquarters in the United States. Business management and operations is a major part of the economy. The Metroplex also contains the largest
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Information_Technology" title="Information Technology">
        Information Technology
       </a>
       industry base in the state (often referred to as
       <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Prairie" title="Silicon Prairie">
        Silicon Prairie
       </a>
       or the
       <a href="/wiki/Telecom_Corridor" title="Telecom Corridor">
        Telecom Corridor
       </a>
       , especially when referring to US-75 through
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richardson,_TX" title="Richardson, TX">
        Richardson
       </a>
       just north of Dallas itself). This area has a large number of corporate IT projects and the presence of numerous electronics, computing and telecommunication firms such as
       <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">
        Microsoft
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Texas_Instruments" title="Texas Instruments">
        Texas Instruments
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HP_Enterprise_Services" title="HP Enterprise Services">
        HP Enterprise Services
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dell_Services" title="Dell Services">
        Dell Services
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">
        Nokia
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/I2_Technologies" title="I2 Technologies">
        i2
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AT%26T_Inc." title="AT&amp;T Inc.">
        AT&amp;T
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alcatel-Lucent" title="Alcatel-Lucent">
        Alcatel-Lucent
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ericsson" title="Ericsson">
        Ericsson
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/CA_Technologies" title="CA Technologies">
        CA
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">
        Google
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Verizon" title="Verizon">
        Verizon
       </a>
       in and around Dallas. On the other end of the business spectrum, and on the other side of the Metroplex, the Texas
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Farming" title="Farming">
        farming
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ranching" title="Ranching">
        ranching
       </a>
       industry is based in Fort Worth. According to the
       <i>
        Dallas Business Journal
       </i>
       <span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">
        '
       </span>
       s 2006 Book of Lists,
       <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">
        American Airlines
       </a>
       is the largest employer in the Metroplex. Several major defense manufacturers, including
       <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">
        Lockheed Martin
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bell_Helicopter_Textron" title="Bell Helicopter Textron">
        Bell Helicopter Textron
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Raytheon" title="Raytheon">
        Raytheon
       </a>
       , maintain significant operations in the Metroplex, primarily on the "Fort Worth side." They are concentrated along State Highway 170 near I-35W, commonly called the "Alliance Corridor" due to its proximity to the Fort Worth Alliance regional airport.
       <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil" title="ExxonMobil">
        ExxonMobil
       </a>
       , the #2 corporation on the
       <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">
        Fortune 500
       </a>
       listings, is headquartered in
       <a href="/wiki/Irving,_Texas" title="Irving, Texas">
        Irving, Texas
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Motor_Sales,_U.S.A.,_Inc." title="Toyota Motor Sales, U.S.A., Inc.">
        Toyota USA
       </a>
       , in 2016, relocated its corporate headquarters to
       <a href="/wiki/Plano,_Texas" title="Plano, Texas">
        Plano, Texas
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Airlines" title="Southwest Airlines">
        Southwest Airlines
       </a>
       hold their headquarters in Dallas. The airline has more than 53,000 employees as of October 2016 and operates more than 3,900 departures a day during peak travel season. In October 2016,
       <a href="/wiki/Jacobs_Engineering_Group" title="Jacobs Engineering Group">
        Jacobs Engineering
       </a>
       , a Fortune 500 company and one of the world’s largest engineering companies, relocated from
       <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_California" title="Pasadena, California">
        Pasadena, California
       </a>
       to Dallas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Changes in
       <a href="/wiki/House_price_index" title="House price index">
        house prices
       </a>
       for the Metroplex are publicly tracked on a regular basis using the
       <a href="/wiki/Case%E2%80%93Shiller_index" title="Case–Shiller index">
        Case–Shiller index
       </a>
       ; the statistic is published by
       <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" title="Standard &amp; Poor's">
        Standard &amp; Poor's
       </a>
       and is also a component of S&amp;P's 20-city
       <a href="/wiki/Composite_(finance)" title="Composite (finance)">
        composite index
       </a>
       of the value of the U.S. residential real estate market.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Higher_education">
        Higher education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">

       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Politics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="toccolours" style="float:right; margin:1em 0 1em 1em; font-size:95%;">

      <p>
       Since the late 20th century and the realignment of party affiliations, white conservatives have shifted to the Republican Party, and its national candidates have won in the Dallas-Fort Worth area, including in presidential elections. Democratic voters dominate a majority of areas in the large cities of Dallas, Fort Worth, Grand Prairie, and Arlington (especially areas east of Interstate 35W).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Republicans dominate North Dallas, western Fort Worth and the rest of Tarrant County, most suburbs, and the rural areas of the Metroplex.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">
        Transportation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Transportation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth-area_freeways" title="List of Dallas–Fort Worth-area freeways">
        List of Dallas–Fort Worth-area freeways
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">

          </a>

        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">

          <span class="hide-when-compact">

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dallas_-_Fort_Worth_International_Airport.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Dallas_-_Fort_Worth_International_Airport.jpg/220px-Dallas_-_Fort_Worth_International_Airport.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Dallas_-_Fort_Worth_International_Airport.jpg/330px-Dallas_-_Fort_Worth_International_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Dallas_-_Fort_Worth_International_Airport.jpg/440px-Dallas_-_Fort_Worth_International_Airport.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dallas_-_Fort_Worth_International_Airport.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Dallas/Fort_Worth_International_Airport" title="Dallas/Fort Worth International Airport">
          Dallas/Fort Worth International Airport
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Dallas/Fort_Worth_International_Airport" title="Dallas/Fort Worth International Airport">
        Dallas/Fort Worth International Airport
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">
        IATA airport code
       </a>
       : DFW), located between the cities of Dallas and Fort Worth, is the largest and busiest airport in the state of
       <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">
        Texas
       </a>
       . At 100 square kilometres (39 sq mi) of total land area, DFW is the second-largest airport in the country and sixth-largest in the world. It is the third-busiest airport in the world in terms of aircraft movements and the seventh-busiest airport in the world in terms of passenger traffic, transporting 62.9 million passengers in FY 2014.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">
        American Airlines
       </a>
       , based in Fort Worth, has its headquarters adjacent to DFW Airport. American, which recently regained the title as largest airline in the world in terms of passengers transported and fleet size, is a predominant leader in domestic routes and operations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Love_Field" title="Dallas Love Field">
        Love Field
       </a>
       Airport (IATA airport code: DAL) is located on the northwest side of the city of Dallas.
       <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Airlines" title="Southwest Airlines">
        Southwest Airlines
       </a>
       is based in Dallas next to Love Field.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:502px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dallas-Fort_Worth_Metroplex_Rail_Transit_Services.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4444" data-file-width="7726" height="288" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Dallas-Fort_Worth_Metroplex_Rail_Transit_Services.png/500px-Dallas-Fort_Worth_Metroplex_Rail_Transit_Services.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Dallas-Fort_Worth_Metroplex_Rail_Transit_Services.png/750px-Dallas-Fort_Worth_Metroplex_Rail_Transit_Services.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Dallas-Fort_Worth_Metroplex_Rail_Transit_Services.png/1000px-Dallas-Fort_Worth_Metroplex_Rail_Transit_Services.png 2x" width="500"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dallas-Fort_Worth_Metroplex_Rail_Transit_Services.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Diagram of public rail transit in the Dallas/Fort Worth area
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Public transit options continue to expand significantly, however, it is limited in several outlying and rural suburbs. Dallas County and parts of Collin and Rockwall counties have bus service and
       <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">
        light rail
       </a>
       operated by
       <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Area_Rapid_Transit" title="Dallas Area Rapid Transit">
        Dallas Area Rapid Transit
       </a>
       (DART), covering thirteen member cities. DART's rail network currently sprawls for 93 miles throughout the area. The Red Line extends north to Plano and southwest to Westmoreland Road. The Blue Line reaches from Rowlett in the northeast to the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Texas_at_Dallas" title="University of North Texas at Dallas">
        University of North Texas at Dallas
       </a>
       campus near I-20 in the south. The 28-mile Green Line, which opened in December 2010, connects Carrollton in the northwest through Downtown Dallas to Pleasant Grove in the southeast. The Orange Line, which completed expansion in 2014, parallels the Red Line from Plano to Downtown Dallas and the Green Line from Downtown Dallas to Northwest Hwy before extending through the Las Colinas area of Irving to reach DFW International Airport.
      </p>
      <p>
       Denton County has bus service limited to Denton, Highland Village, and Lewisville (with commuter service to downtown Dallas) provided by the
       <a href="/wiki/Denton_County_Transportation_Authority" title="Denton County Transportation Authority">
        Denton County Transportation Authority
       </a>
       (DCTA). The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A-train_(Denton_County_Transportation_Authority)" title="A-train (Denton County Transportation Authority)">
        A-train
       </a>
       , a diesel commuter rail line, parallels
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_35E_(Texas)" title="Interstate 35E (Texas)">
        I-35E
       </a>
       to connect Denton, Highland Village, Lewisville, and Carrollton. Several smaller towns along this line, Corinth, Shady Shores, and Lake Dallas, voted to abstain from DCTA and do not have stations. There is an across-the-platform transfer in Carrollton to the DART Green Line. A-Train service began June 20, 2011.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opening_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-opening-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Tarrant County has bus service operated by the
       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Worth_Transportation_Authority" title="Fort Worth Transportation Authority">
        Fort Worth Transportation Authority
       </a>
       (known as 'The T'), available only in Fort Worth. The diesel commuter train that serves Fort Worth and its eastern suburbs is operated as the
       <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Railway_Express" title="Trinity Railway Express">
        Trinity Railway Express
       </a>
       ; it connects downtown Fort Worth to downtown Dallas, where it links to the DART light rail system. A station near its midpoint, Centerport, serves DFW Airport via a free airport shuttle bus. The TRE is jointly owned by FWTA and DART.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">
        Amtrak
       </a>
       serves Dallas and Fort Worth once daily in each direction on a route from Chicago to
       <a href="/wiki/Austin,_Texas" title="Austin, Texas">
        Austin
       </a>
       to San Antonio, with connections at San Antonio to New Orleans, Houston, El Paso, Phoenix, and Los Angeles.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Dallas-Fort Worth area has thousands of lane-miles of freeways and interstates. The Metroplex has the second-largest number of freeway-miles per capita in the nation, behind only the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Metropolitan_Area" title="Kansas City Metropolitan Area">
        Kansas City Metropolitan Area
       </a>
       . As in most major metropolitan areas in Texas, most interstates and freeways have access or frontage roads where most of the businesses are located; these access roads have slip ramps allowing traffic to transition between the freeway and access road. North-south interstates include
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_35_(Texas)" title="Interstate 35 (Texas)">
        I-35
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_45_(Texas)" title="Interstate 45 (Texas)">
        I-45
       </a>
       . East-west routes include
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_30_(Texas)" title="Interstate 30 (Texas)">
        I-30
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_20_(Texas)" title="Interstate 20 (Texas)">
        I-20
       </a>
       . I-35 splits into
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_35E_(Texas)" title="Interstate 35E (Texas)">
        I-35E
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_35W_(Texas)" title="Interstate 35W (Texas)">
        I-35W
       </a>
       from Denton to Hillsboro: I-35W goes through Fort Worth while I-35E goes through Dallas. (This is one of only two examples of an interstate splitting off into branches and then rejoining as one; the other such split is in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minneapolis-St._Paul" title="Minneapolis-St. Paul">
        Minneapolis-St. Paul
       </a>
       where I-35E goes into
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Paul,_Minnesota" title="St. Paul, Minnesota">
        St. Paul
       </a>
       and I-35W goes through
       <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis" title="Minneapolis">
        Minneapolis
       </a>
       .)
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_30_(Texas)" title="Interstate 30 (Texas)">
        I-30
       </a>
       connects Dallas and Fort Worth, and I-45 connects Dallas to Houston. The "multiple-of-5" numbers used for the interstate designations are notable, as these numbers were designed to be used for major multi-state arteries of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Interstate_Highway_System" title="U.S. Interstate Highway System">
        U.S. Interstate Highway System
       </a>
       . The North Texas region is the terminus for two of them, and I-45 is located only within Texas.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/High-occupancy_vehicle_lane" title="High-occupancy vehicle lane">
        HOV lanes
       </a>
       exist along I-35E, I-30,
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_635_(Texas)" title="Interstate 635 (Texas)">
        I-635
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_67" title="U.S. Route 67">
        US 67
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Highway_75_(Texas)" title="U.S. Highway 75 (Texas)">
        US 75
       </a>
       . I-20 bypasses both Dallas and Fort Worth to the south while its loop,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_820_(Texas)" title="Interstate 820 (Texas)">
        I-820
       </a>
       , goes around Fort Worth.
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_635_(Texas)" title="Interstate 635 (Texas)">
        I-635
       </a>
       splits to the north of I-20 and loops around east and north Dallas, ending at
       <a href="/wiki/Texas_State_Highway_121" title="Texas State Highway 121">
        SH 121
       </a>
       north of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dallas-Fort_Worth_International_Airport" title="Dallas-Fort Worth International Airport">
        DFW Airport
       </a>
       . I-35E,
       <a href="/wiki/Texas_State_Highway_Loop_12" title="Texas State Highway Loop 12">
        Loop 12
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Texas_State_Highway_Spur_408" title="Texas State Highway Spur 408">
        Spur 408
       </a>
       ultimately connect to I-20 southwest of Dallas, completing the west bypass loop around Dallas. A large number of construction projects are planned or are already underway in the region to alleviate congestion. Due largely to funding issues, many of the new projects involve building new tollways or adding tolled express lanes to existing highways, which are managed by the
       <a href="/wiki/North_Texas_Tollway_Authority" title="North Texas Tollway Authority">
        North Texas Tollway Authority
       </a>
       . It was originally established to manage the
       <a href="/wiki/Dallas_North_Tollway" title="Dallas North Tollway">
        Dallas North Tollway
       </a>
       and oversees several other toll projects in the area.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As of 2016 the Taiwanese airline
       <a href="/wiki/EVA_Air" title="EVA Air">
        EVA Air
       </a>
       operates a shuttle bus service from
       <a href="/wiki/George_Bush_Intercontinental_Airport" title="George Bush Intercontinental Airport">
        George Bush Intercontinental Airport
       </a>
       in Houston to
       <a href="/wiki/Richardson,_Texas" title="Richardson, Texas">
        Richardson
       </a>
       , so that Dallas-based customers may fly on its services to and from Houston.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">
        Media
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Media">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The cities of Dallas and Fort Worth have their own newspapers,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Dallas_Morning_News" title="The Dallas Morning News">
         The Dallas Morning News
        </a>
       </i>
       and the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Fort_Worth_Star-Telegram" title="Fort Worth Star-Telegram">
         Fort Worth Star-Telegram
        </a>
       </i>
       , respectively. Historically, the two papers had readership primarily in their own counties.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       As the two cities' suburbs have grown together in recent years (and especially since the demise of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Times_Herald" title="Dallas Times Herald">
         Dallas Times Herald
        </a>
       </i>
       in 1991), many sites sell both papers. This pattern of crossover has been repeated in other print media, radio, and television. Since the 1970s all of the television stations and most of the FM radio stations have chosen to transmit from
       <a href="/wiki/Cedar_Hill,_Texas" title="Cedar Hill, Texas">
        Cedar Hill
       </a>
       so as to serve the entire market, and are programmed likewise. There has been a rise in "
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=FCC_docket_80-90&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="FCC docket 80-90 (page does not exist)">
        80–90
       </a>
       move-ins", whereby stations have been moved from distant markets, in some cases as far away as Oklahoma, and relicensed to anonymous small towns in the Metroplex to serve as additional DFW stations. According to
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RadioTime" title="RadioTime">
         RadioTime
        </a>
        ,
       </i>
       the market has 38
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AM_band" title="AM band">
        AM
       </a>
       stations, 58
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FM_band" title="FM band">
        FM
       </a>
       stations (many of them
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_broadcast_station_classes" title="List of broadcast station classes">
        class Cs
       </a>
       ), and 18 full-power television stations. Dallas-Fort Worth is the fifth-largest television market in the United States, behind only New York City, Los Angeles, Chicago, and Philadelphia.
      </p>
      <p>
       Two Metroplex AM radio stations, 820
       <a href="/wiki/WBAP_(AM)" title="WBAP (AM)">
        WBAP
       </a>
       and 1080
       <a href="/wiki/KRLD_(AM)" title="KRLD (AM)">
        KRLD
       </a>
       , are 50,000-watt stations with coverage of much of the North American continent and beyond during nighttime hours.
      </p>
      <p>
       The South Asian population (Indian Sub-continent) has increased considerably in the DFW metroplex. They have the FM 104.9 radio channel and 700 AM radio.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Recently Sony TV, a subsidiary of Sony TV Asia, launched its FTA (free to Air OTA) channel on 44.2 station in DFW. It was one of the two locations they chose in USA; the other being NYC, where there is also a large South Asian demographic.
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_Stations">
        Radio Stations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Radio Stations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Category:Radio_stations_in_the_Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex" title="Category:Radio stations in the Dallas–Fort Worth metroplex">
         Category:Radio stations in the Dallas–Fort Worth metroplex
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
        Sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The Metroplex is one of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._cities_with_teams_from_four_major_sports" title="U.S. cities with teams from four major sports">
        twelve American metropolitan areas
       </a>
       that has a team in each of the four major professional sports leagues. Major professional sports first came to the area in 1960, when the
       <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Cowboys" title="Dallas Cowboys">
        Dallas Cowboys
       </a>
       began competing in the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">
        National Football League
       </a>
       and the Dallas Texans began competing in the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Football_League" title="American Football League">
        American Football League
       </a>
       . (The Texans later relocated to
       <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City,_Missouri" title="Kansas City, Missouri">
        Kansas City
       </a>
       and became the
       <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Chiefs" title="Kansas City Chiefs">
        Chiefs
       </a>
       ). In 1972,
       <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">
        Major League Baseball's
       </a>
       Washington Senators moved to Arlington to become the
       <a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">
        Texas Rangers
       </a>
       , named after the
       <a href="/wiki/Texas_Ranger_Division" title="Texas Ranger Division">
        statewide law enforcement agency
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">
        National Basketball Association
       </a>
       expanded into North Texas in 1980 when the
       <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Mavericks" title="Dallas Mavericks">
        Dallas Mavericks
       </a>
       were added to the league. The fourth sport was added in 1993 when the
       <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_North_Stars" title="Minnesota North Stars">
        Minnesota North Stars
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">
        National Hockey League
       </a>
       moved to Dallas, becoming the
       <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Stars" title="Dallas Stars">
        Dallas Stars
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">
        Major League Soccer
       </a>
       team
       <a href="/wiki/FC_Dallas" title="FC Dallas">
        FC Dallas
       </a>
       is based in Frisco, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Wings" title="Dallas Wings">
        Dallas Wings
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_National_Basketball_Association" title="Women's National Basketball Association">
        WNBA
       </a>
       play in Arlington. The area is also home to many minor-league professional teams, and four colleges that compete in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA">
        NCAA
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">
        Division I
       </a>
       athletics. The Metroplex has hosted many premiere sports events on both an annual and one-time basis.
      </p>

      <p>
       The headquarters for both the Big 12 and Conference USA are located in
       <a href="/wiki/Irving,_Texas" title="Irving, Texas">
        Irving
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Southland_Conference" title="Southland Conference">
        Southland Conference
       </a>
       headquarters are in
       <a href="/wiki/Frisco,_Texas" title="Frisco, Texas">
        Frisco
       </a>
       .
      </p>
